{"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_013qBcPDG3CDaHEoJUrE8aSs","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"thinking","thinking":"Perfect! Now I can see the structure. The `acpi_video_get_backlight_type()` function follows this logic:\n\n1. First check command-line args (acpi_backlight_cmdline)\n2. Then check DMI quirks (acpi_backlight_dmi) via the `video_detect_dmi_table`\n3. Then auto-detect based on whether ACPI video backlight is supported\n4. If on Win8 with a native backlight device, use native\n5. Otherwise use ACPI video\n\nThe bug report shows that on the Acer TravelMate 5735Z:\n- Default behavior is broken (using the wrong backlight driver)\n- With `acpi_backlight=native`, it works correctly\n- The system has acer-wmi and intel_backlight drivers available\n\nLooking at the acer-wmi.c file earlier, I saw there's a `video_vendor_dmi_table` that's checked, but apparently the Acer TravelMate 5735Z is not in this table or in the main backlight detection table.\n\nThe problem is that the system defaults to acpi_backlight_video when it should be using acpi_backlight_native. This is happening because:\n1. The BIOS reports ACPI video backlight support\n2. The system is not Win8-ready (so the Win8 check doesn't help)\n3. Therefore it falls through to using acpi_backlight_video\n\nThe fix would be to add the Acer TravelMate 5735Z to the `video_detect_dmi_table` with a callback to force it to use `acpi_backlight_native`.\n\nLet me search to see if there's already an entry for this
